silicon&#8221; was announced earlier this year at WWDC, with Tim Cook describing it as &#8220;a historic day for the Mac.&#8221; But now we&#8217;ll actually get some product 13:31:19","updatedTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:19","title":"REEF Technology raises $700M from SoftBank and others to remake parking lots","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2069061","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">It seems like <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/softbank\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"softbank\">SoftBank <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and the Mubadala Corp. aren&#8217;t finished taking big swings at the commercial real estate business in the U.S. Even after the collapse of WeWork, the investors are doubling down on a similar business model as part of a syndicate investing $700 million into <a href=\"https://reeftechnology.com/\">REEF Technology</a>.</p>\n<p>REEF began its life as Miami-based ParkJockey, providing hardware, software and management services for parking lots. It has since expanded its vision while remaining true to its basic business model. While it still manages parking lots, it now it adds infrastructure for cloud kitchens, healthcare clinics, logistics and last-mile delivery, and even old school brick and mortar retail and experiential consumer spaces on top of those now-empty parking structures and spaces.</p>\n<p>Like WeWork, REEF leases most of the real estate it operates and upgrades it before leasing it to other occupants (or using the spaces itself). Unlike WeWork, the business actually has a fair shot at working out &#8212; especially given business trends that have accelerated in response to the health and safety measures implemented to stop the spread of the COVID-19 pandemic.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>In part that&#8217;s because REEF does operate its own businesses on the premises and works with startups to provide actual goods and services that are location dependent for their success and revenue generating.</p>\n<p>The money will be used to scale from its roughly 4,800 locations to 10,000 new locations around the country and to transform the parking lots into &#8220;neighborhood hubs,&#8221; according to Ari Ojalvo, the company&#8217;s co-founder and chief executive.</p>\n<p>SoftBank and Mubadala are joining private equity and financial investment giants Oaktree, UBS Asset Management and the European venture capital firm Target Global in providing the cash for the massive equity financing. Meanwhile, <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/reef-technology\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"reef-technology\">REEF Technology <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and Oaktree are collaborating on a $300 million real estate investment vehicle, the Neighborhood Property Group,<a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-11-02/oaktree-reef-technology-launch-300-million-property-fund\"> as Bloomberg reported on Monday</a>.</p>\n<p>In all, REEF, which could reasonably be described as a WeWork for the neighborhood store, has $1 billion in capital coming to build out what it calls a proximity-as-a-service platform.</p>\n<p>Since taking a minority investment from SoftBank back in 2018 (an investment which reportedly valued the company at $1 billion) and transforming from ParkJockey into REEF Technology, the company added a booming cloud kitchen business to support the increase in virtual restaurant chains.</p>\n<p>In addition, it added a number of service providers as partners,<span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\"> including</span><a style=\"background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\" href=\"https://venturebeat.com/2020/01/28/bond-raises-15-million-to-bring-last-mile-deliveries-and-nano-distribution-centers-to-online-retailers/\"> last-mile delivery startup</a><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\"> </span><a style=\"background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\" href=\"https://www.withbond.com/\">Bond</a><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\"> (and the logistics giant, DHL); </span><a style=\"background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\" href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/10/carbon-health-to-launch-100-pop-up-covid-19-testing-clinics-across-the-u-s/\">the national primary healthcare services clinic operator</a><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\"> and technology developer, </span><a style=\"background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\" href=\"https://carbonhealth.com/\">Carbon Health</a><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">; the electric vehicle charging and maintenance provider, </span><a style=\"background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\" href=\"https://www.charge.us/\">Get Charged</a><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">; and &#8212; at its operations in London &#8212; the new vertical farm developer, </span><a style=\"background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\" href=\"http://www.cratetoplate.farm/\">Crate to Plate</a><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\"> (Ojalvo said it was in talks with the established vertical farming companies in the U.S. on potential partnerships).</span></p>\n<p>Next year, the company plans to launch the first of its experiential, open-air entertainment venues at a space it operates in Austin, according to Ojalvo.</p>\n<p>And further down the road, the company sees an opportunity to serve as a hub for the kinds of data-processing centers and telecommunications gateways that will power the smart city of the 21st century, Ojalvo said.</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&#8220;We have inbound interest from companies that do edge computing and companies getting ready with 5G,&#8221; he said. &#8220;Data and infrastructure is a big part of our neighborhood hub. It’s like electricity. Without electricity and connectivity, we don’t have the world we want to see.&#8221; </span></p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2002397\" style=\"width: 5474px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2002397\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2002397 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/vehicles-GettyImages-1215795874.jpg\" alt=\"Rental Cars Stored At Dodger Stadium During Coronavirus Pandemic\" width=\"5464\" height=\"3640\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/vehicles-GettyImages-1215795874.jpg 5464w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/vehicles-GettyImages-1215795874.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/vehicles-GettyImages-1215795874.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/vehicles-GettyImages-1215795874.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/vehicles-GettyImages-1215795874.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/vehicles-GettyImages-1215795874.jpg?resize=1536,1023 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/vehicles-GettyImages-1215795874.jpg?resize=2048,1364 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/06/vehicles-GettyImages-1215795874.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 5464px) 100vw, 5464px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2002397\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Rental cars are stored in a parking lot at Dodger Stadium in this aerial photograph taken over Los Angeles, California, U.S., on Wednesday, May 27, 2020. Hertz Global Holdings Inc. will sell as many of its rental cars as possible while in bankruptcy to bring its huge fleet in line with reduced future demand in a post-pandemic economy.</p></div></p>\n<p>The bulk of the company&#8217;s revenue is coming from its parking business, but Ojalvo expects that to change as the its cloud kitchen business continues to grow. &#8220;Neighborhood Kitchens will be a significant part of non-parking revenue,&#8221; said Ojalvo.</p>\n<p>REEF already operates more than 100 Neighborhood Kitchens across more than 20 markets in North America, and that number will only grow as the company expands its regional footprint. It&#8217;s hosting virtual kitchens from celebrity chefs like David Chang&#8217;s <a href=\"https://eatfuku.com/\">Fuku</a>, and, according to the company, offering lifelines to beloved local restaurateurs like the chain <a href=\"http://jackswifefreda.com/\">Jack&#8217;s Wife Freda</a> in New York or <a href=\"http://www.chefmichellebernstein.com/\">Michelle Bernstein&#8217;s kitchens</a> in Miami.</p>\n<p>These restaurants are, in some cases, taking advantage of the employees that REEF Technology has operating its network of kitchens. It&#8217;s another difference between WeWork and REEF. The company not only provides the space, in many instances it&#8217;s providing the labor that&#8217;s allowing businesses to scale.</p>\n<p>The company already employs over a thousand kitchen workers prepping food at its restaurants. And REEF acquired a company earlier in May to consolidate its back-end service for on-demand deliveries.</p>\n<p>That same strategy will likely apply to other aspects of the company&#8217;s services, as well.</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&#8220;We’re building a platform of proximity,&#8221; says Ojalvo. &#8220;That proximity is driven through an install base that’s in parking lots or parking garages… [and] that enables all sorts of companies to use its proximity as a platform. To basically build their marketplaces.&#8221;</span></p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1829017\" style=\"width: 2004px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1829017\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-1829017 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/deliveroo2.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1994\" height=\"1064\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/deliveroo2.jpg 1994w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/deliveroo2.jpg?resize=150,80 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/deliveroo2.jpg?resize=300,160 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/deliveroo2.jpg?resize=768,410 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/deliveroo2.jpg?resize=680,363 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/deliveroo2.jpg?resize=1536,820 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/05/deliveroo2.jpg?resize=50,27 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1994px) 100vw, 1994px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-1829017\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">CARDIFF, UNITED KINGDOM &#8211; DECEMBER 22: A Deliveroo rider at work at night on December 22, 2018 in Cardiff, United Kingdom. (Photo by Matthew Horwood/Getty Images)</p></div></p>\n<p>As REEF raises money for expansion, it&#8217;s tapping into a new theory of urban development embraced by mayors from Amsterdam to Tempe, Ariz. calling for a 15-minute city (one where the amenities needed for a comfortable urban existence are no more than 15 minutes away).</p>\n<p>It&#8217;s a worthwhile goal, but while mayors seem to place the emphasis on the availability of accessible amenities, REEF&#8217;s leadership acknowledges that only a few of its parking lots and garages will be multi-use and accessible to neighborhood residents. According to a spokesman, only several hundred of the company&#8217;s planned 10,000 businesses will have the kind of multi-use mall environment that encourages neighborhood access. Instead, its business seems to be based on the notion that most delivery services should be no more than 15 minutes away.</p>\n<p>It&#8217;s a different project, but it also has a number of supporters. One could argue that cloud kitchen providers like Zuul, Kitchen United, and Travis Kalanick&#8217;s Cloud Kitchens all ascribe to the same belief. Kalanick, the Uber co-founder and former CEO whose company received billions from SoftBank, has been snapping up properties in the US and Asia under an investment vehicle called City Storage Systems, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/uber-founder-travis-kalanicks-new-company-turns-parking-lots-and-abandoned-shopping-malls-into-space-for-businesses-2018-3\">which also uses parking lots and abandoned malls as fulfillment centers</a>.</p>\n<p>Big retailers also have taken notice of the new revenue stream and one of America&#8217;s largest, Kroger, is even running a ghost kitchen experiment in the Midwest.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"W2dflHeUpQ\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/08/kroger-one-of-americas-largest-grocery-chains-experiments-with-ghost-kitchens-and-delivery-in-the-midwest/\">Kroger, one of America&#8217;s largest grocery chains, experiments with ghost kitchens and delivery in the Midwest</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Kroger, one of America&#8217;s largest grocery chains, experiments with ghost kitchens and delivery in the Midwest&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/08/kroger-one-of-americas-largest-grocery-chains-experiments-with-ghost-kitchens-and-delivery-in-the-midwest/embed/#?secret=W2dflHeUpQ\" data-secret=\"W2dflHeUpQ\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>If that&#8217;s not enough, there are plenty of under-utilized assets that are already on the market thanks to the economic downturn wrought by the COVID-19 pandemic and the government&#8217;s efforts to contain it.</p>\n<p>&#8220;I guess a lot depends on how you think delivery players work out in the coming years versus say drive through or curbside pickup which seems to be where large national players are focused (Starbucks, McDonalds, Dominos, etc),&#8221; wrote on venture investor in an email. &#8220;But how do delivery players use these spaces versus say lots of low cost retail spaces that can be used to staging or package returns. Maybe there is a play to add modular or prefab units to the existing parking spaces on provide flex for scaling, but it&#8217;s not clear that anyone is growing at a frantic pace&#8230; I&#8217;m just not sure how to see converted parking versus other&#8230; commercial spaces for retail or office that are all searching for new applications.&#8221;</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2069089\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2069089\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2069089 size-large\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-02-at-10.05.26-PM.png?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"361\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-02-at-10.05.26-PM.png 2536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-02-at-10.05.26-PM.png?resize=150,80 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-02-at-10.05.26-PM.png?resize=300,159 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-02-at-10.05.26-PM.png?resize=768,408 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-02-at-10.05.26-PM.png?resize=680,361 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-02-at-10.05.26-PM.png?resize=1536,816 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-02-at-10.05.26-PM.png?resize=2048,1089 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-02-at-10.05.26-PM.png?resize=50,27 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2069089\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">REEF Technology last mile delivery vehicle and DHL-branded vehicle. Image Credit: <a href=\"https://www.reeftechnology.com\">REEF Technology</a></p></div></p>\n<p>The COVID-19 outbreak that has changed so much of modern life in America so quickly in the span of a single year didn&#8217;t create the urge to transform the urban environment, but it did much to accelerate it.</p>\n<p>As REEF acknowledges, cities are the future.</p>\n<p>Roughly two-thirds of the world&#8217;s population will live in cities by 2050, and the world&#8217;s largest cities are cracking under the pressures of economic, civil, and environmental transformations that they have not been able to address effectively.</p>\n<p>Mobility and, by extension, places to store and maintain those mobile technologies are part of the problem. Roughly half of the average modern American city, as REEF notes, is devoted to parking, while parks occupy only 10% of urban spaces. REEF&#8217;s language is centered on changing a world of parking lots into a space of paradises, but that language belies a reality that makes its money (at least for now) off of isolating individuals into personal spaces where their commercial needs are met by delivery &#8212; not by community interaction.</p>\n<p>Still, the fact remains that something needs to change.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Traditional developers and local policies have been slow to adopt new technologies and operating models,&#8221; said Stonly Baptiste, an investor in the transformation of urban environments through the fund, Urban.Us (which is not a backer of REEF). &#8220;But the demand is growing for a better &#8216;city product&#8217;, the need to make cities better for the environment and our lives has never been greater, and the dream to build the city of the future never dies. Not that dream is subsidized by VC.&#8221;</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=CS_C-HuY3aU:iM4E6lJg0z0:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img 13:31:19","updatedTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:19","title":"AWS launches its next-gen GPU instances","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2069013","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">AWS today <a href=\"https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/aws/new-gpu-equipped-ec2-p4-instances-for-machine-learning-hpc/\">announced</a> the launch of its newest GPU-equipped instances. Dubbed P4, these <a href=\"https://aws.amazon.com/ec2/instance-types/p4/\">new instances</a> are launching a decade after AWS launched its first set of Cluster GPU instances. This new generation is powered by Intel Cascade Lake processors and eight of Nvidia&#8217;s A100 Tensor Core GPUs. These instances, AWS promises, offer up to 2.5x the deep learning performance of the previous generation &#8212; and training a comparable model should be about 60% cheaper with these new instances.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2069025\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Graphic@2x-nividia-30.png\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2069025\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2069025\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Graphic@2x-nividia-30.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"731\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Graphic@2x-nividia-30.png 1340w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Graphic@2x-nividia-30.png?resize=150,107 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Graphic@2x-nividia-30.png?resize=300,214 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Graphic@2x-nividia-30.png?resize=768,548 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Graphic@2x-nividia-30.png?resize=680,485 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Graphic@2x-nividia-30.png?resize=50,36 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2069025\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> AWS</p></div></p>\n<p>For now, there is only one size available, <a href=\"https://pages.awscloud.com/amazon-ec2-p4d.html\">the p4d.12xlarge instance</a>, in AWS slang, and the eight A100 GPUs are connected over Nvidia&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.nvidia.com/en-us/data-center/nvlink/\">NVLink communication interface</a> and offer support for the company&#8217;s <a href=\"https://developer.nvidia.com/gpudirect\">GPUDirect interface</a> as well.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>With 320 GB of high-bandwidth GPU memory and 400 Gbps networking, this is obviously a very powerful machine. Add to that the 96 CPU cores, 1.1 TB of system memory and 8 TB of SSD storage and it&#8217;s maybe no surprise that the on-demand price is $32.77 per hour (though that price goes down to less than $20/hour for one-year reserved instances and $11.57 for three-year reserved instances.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2069024\" style=\"width: 900px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/p4d_ultracluister_1.png\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2069024\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2069024\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/p4d_ultracluister_1.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"890\" height=\"608\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/p4d_ultracluister_1.png 890w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/p4d_ultracluister_1.png?resize=150,102 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/p4d_ultracluister_1.png?resize=300,205 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/p4d_ultracluister_1.png?resize=768,525 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/p4d_ultracluister_1.png?resize=680,465 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/p4d_ultracluister_1.png?resize=50,34 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 890px) 100vw, 890px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2069024\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> AWS</p></div></p>\n<p>On the extreme end, you can combine 4,000 or more GPUs into <a href=\"https://aws.amazon.com/about-aws/whats-new/2020/11/announcing-new-amazon-ec2-p4d-instances/\">an EC2 UltraCluster</a>, as AWS calls these machines, for high-performance computing workloads at what is essentially a supercomputer-scale machine. Given the price, you&#8217;re not likely to spin up one of these clusters to train your model for your toy app anytime soon, but AWS has already been working with a number of enterprise customers to test these instances and clusters, including Toyota Research Institute, GE Healthcare and Aon.</p>\n<p><iframe class='youtube-player' width='640' height='360' src='https://www.youtube.com/embed/-zqlan5sqio?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;fs=1&#038;autohide=2&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;wmode=transparent' allowfullscreen='true' style='border:0;'></iframe></p>\n<p style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&#8220;At [<a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/toyota-research-institute\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"toyota-research-institute\">Toyota Research Institute], <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> we&#8217;re working to build a future where everyone has the freedom to move,&#8221; said Mike Garrison, Technical Lead, Infrastructure Engineering at TRI. &#8220;The previous generation P3 instances helped us reduce our time to train machine learning models from days to hours and we are looking forward to utilizing P4d instances, as the additional GPU memory and more efficient float formats will allow our machine learning team to train with more complex models at an even faster speed.&#8221;</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"WTHeRQVTyB\"><p><a 13:31:19","updatedTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:19","title":"Scaleway launches cloud instances that cost $2.10 per month","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2068870","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">French cloud hosting company <a href=\"https://www.scaleway.com/en/\">Scaleway</a> originally started with <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2015/09/02/scaleway-now-provides-crazy-cheap-virtual-private-servers-starting-at-3-40-per-month/\">very cheap</a> cloud instances. Over the years, the company has expanded its offering and added more premium services, such as managed Kubernetes, object storage, block storage, managed databases, load balancers and GPU instances. But Scaleway is now launching <a href=\"https://www.scaleway.com/en/stardust-instances/\">another cheap cloud instance</a> that costs €0.0025 per hour — around $0.0039 per hour.</p>\n<p>Obviously, you’re not getting incredible performance for that price. But it’s a good way to try out new things and build an application just for you. If you’re the only user, those specifications might be enough.</p>\n<p>Called Stardust, the virtual compute instance comes with 1 vCPU, 1GB of RAM, an IP address (IPv4), 10GB of local storage and <em>up to</em> 100Mbps of bandwidth. There’s no restriction on bandwidth usage.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Billed by the hour, you end up paying €1.80 per month ($2.10). The company isn’t going to generate a ton of revenue from such a cheap product. That’s why supply is limited. <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/scaleway\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"scaleway\">Scaleway <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> will release a limited batch of cloud instances every month — first come, first served.</p>\n<p>There are also some limits as you can’t spin up a ton of Stardust and build your own infrastructure. Each account can have up to one Stardust instance in Paris and another one in Amsterdam.</p>\n<p>Scaleway lists some potential use cases for its new product, such as an internal wiki, a code repository backup, an always-on instance to set up daemons, triggers and workers, a VPN server, etc. The instance supports Ubuntu, Debian, CentOS and Fedora.</p>\n<div class=\"embed src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/9a_jFbi6EUE\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 02 Nov 2020 18:37:33 +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI","linkMd5":"fa90cb0bfc37af80522406e87d551a28","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn22@2020_6/2020/11/03/05-31-20-196_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","destWidth":59,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":990,"destBytes":324,"author":"Romain Dillet","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn22@2020_6/2020/11/03/05-31-20-196_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn96@2020_5/2020/11/03/05-31-35-908_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn52@2020_4/2020/11/03/05-31-34-882_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=9a_jFbi6EUE:0fmt8v3MR6o:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn36@2020_1/2020/11/03/05-31-35-774_66f08f5549c50c0c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=9a_jFbi6EUE:0fmt8v3MR6o:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn54@2020_1/2020/11/03/05-31-35-634_9bf8cc42b939bcdc.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn35@2020_5/2020/11/03/05-31-35-960_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/9a_jFbi6EUE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn19@2020_3/2020/11/03/05-31-36-035_769ababb4e67d097.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1604381479577},{"createdTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:19","updatedTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:19","title":"Gillmor Gang: Shaken Not Stirred","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2069076","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><iframe class='youtube-player' width='640' height='360' src='https://www.youtube.com/embed/UIKocxMP4Mg?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;fs=1&#038;autohide=2&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;wmode=transparent' allowfullscreen='true' style='border:0;'></iframe></p>\n<p>With one day to go to the election, our thoughts are with those who look forward to talking about something else. Difficult as it might be to imagine, there must be other things to work on. One thing that comes to mind is the impact of the virus on how we manage our days and nights in a digital environment. Mobile devices have already propelled much of the change, but the pandemic has accelerated the move to a hybrid distributed lifestyle.</p>\n<p>The election has mandated our attention to the political situation in ways that have expanded early voting and legal efforts to slow it down. Regardless of the outcome, the pressure to adapt to this new collaborative workflow will intensify. People have already seen significant shifts from commuting to time switching in a home context. Podcasting, which had emerged from a hackerish geeky hobby in recent years, has morphed into a more commercial adjunct to mainstream media.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>In the process, new formats such as newsletters and live streaming have attracted investment from companies including Spotify and Audible, related technologies like Otter (transcription), Substack, Medium, new bundles of services (Apple One) and cable network disrupters, Digital first publishers like The Recount may have started out as traditional takes on political commentary, but in the windup of the campaign they are reaching audiences via notifications rather than repetitive cable talking heads and panels.</p>\n<p>This roll up of breaking notifications and user-controlled editorial access have major implications for the near future post-electuon, however long it takes to plow through legal challenges and the restaffing of whichever government is formed. Also impacted will be Congressional and antitrust attempts to regulate social media, and what I suspect will be a shift to private discussions and trend analysis. The interest groups and market makers that result from this realignment will offer exit strategies for companies like Twitter and YouTube where the risk of being broken up will be mitigated by powerful new business models for content creation and distribution.</p>\n<p>By January 20th, a new influencer architecture based on notifications and live streaming will endow the media with tools it needs to lead the transition to safe, secure, hybrid digital/live events. Streaming will give new artists and entrepreneurs a platform to separate influence and impact from lossleader gatherings online, bolstered by association with food and tools delivery winners like Apple and Amazon. A similar synergy between tech companies and media advertising will be overt (Apple + and Prime) as well as implicit (the growth in Amazon search.and Twitch watch parties.)</p>\n<p>COVID therapeutics such as Regeneron create a roadmap for these private groups to reorganize as CostCo-like next wave restaurants, entertainment events, and political efforts to consolidate economic power. With a combination of transparency and what could be called reverse boycotts, customers will align with products and companies who promote values-based association with stakeholders acrosss the spectrum.</p>\n<p>Central to the relationship is providing ethical access to important data in return for clear guidelines for the use of that data at scale. If this election has been correctly assessed as signaling a massive change in the electorate, the period of deescalation from the pandemic can foster a sense of ownership of that success by the incoming majority. Notification-based entertainers such as Sarah Cooper and more mainstream projects like Matthew McConaughey’s new book, Greenlights, speak initially to the Zoom home/work crowd, and soon to the formation of new studios and networks.</p>\n<p>Who really knows how this transformation is playing out given the terrible consequences of Trump’s impact on our country and its standing in the world. But the generation that followed the Greatest Generation is discovering it has more to it than the free love of rock and roll and following our bliss. That same generation ushered in the technology and media revolutions.</p>\n<p>Now we’re suffering the backlash of so-called free software where our data is the real product, where Big Brother is extending power by acquihires and preemptive pivots. Yet still our democracy persists. Time to count the vote.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center\">__________________</p>\n<p>The Gillmor Gang — <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/frank-radice\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"frank-radice\">Frank Radice, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/michael-markman-6388\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"michael-markman-6388\">Michael Markman, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/keith-teare\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"keith-teare\">Keith Teare, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/denis-pombriant\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"denis-pombriant\">Denis Pombriant, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/brent-leary\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"brent-leary\">Brent Leary, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/steve-gillmor\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"steve-gillmor\">Steve Gillmor <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a>. goal","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2068937","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Alphabet&#8217;s X (the Google-owner&#8217;s so-called &#8220;Moonshot Factory&#8221;) published a new <a href=\"https://blog.x.company/sharing-project-amber-with-the-mental-health-community-7b6d8814a862\">blog post today</a> about Project Amber, a project it&#8217;s been working on over the past three years &#8212; the results of which it&#8217;s now making available open source for the rest of the mental health research community to learn from, and hopefully build upon. The X project sought to identify a specific biomarker for depression &#8212; it did not accomplish that (and the researchers now believe that a single biomarker for depression and anxiety likely didn&#8217;t exist), but X is still hoping that its work on using electroencephalography (EEG) combined with machine learning to try to find one will be of benefit to others.</p>\n<p>X&#8217;s researchers were hoping that depression, like other ailments and disorders, might have a clear biomarker that would help healthcare professionals more easily and objectively diagnose depression, which would also then hopefully make it more easily and consistently treatable. With EEG, there was some precedent, via studies done in labs using games designed specifically for the purpose, in which people with depression seemed to consistently demonstrate a lower measure of EEG activity in response to effectively &#8220;winning&#8221; the games.</p>\n<p>These studies seemed to offer a path to a potential biomarker, but in order to make them actually useful in real-world diagnostic settings, like a clinic or a public health lab, the team at X set about improving the process of EEG collection and interpretation to make it more accessible, both to users and to technicians.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>What is perhaps most notable about this pursuit, and the post today that Alphabet released detailing its efforts, is that it&#8217;s essentially a story of a years-long investigation that didn&#8217;t work out &#8212; not the side of the moonshot story you typically hear from big tech companies.</p>\n<p>In fact, this is perhaps one of the best examples yet of what critics of many of the approaches of large tech companies fail to understand &#8212; that some problems are not solvable by solutions with analogs in the world of software and engineering.</p>\n<p>The team at X sums up its learnings from the years-long research project in three main bullet points about its user research, and each of them touch in some way on the insufficiency of a pure objective biomarker detection method (even if it had worked), particularly when it comes to mental illness. From the researchers:</p>\n<blockquote>\n<ol>\n<li><strong>Mental health measurement remains an unsolved problem</strong>. Despite the availability of many mental health surveys and scales, they are not widely used, especially in primary care and counseling settings. Reasons range from burden (“I don’t have time for this”) to skepticism (“Using a scale is no better than using my clinical judgement”) to lack of trust (“I don’t think my client is filling this in truthfully” and ”I don’t want to reveal this much to my counsellor”). These findings were in line with the literature on measurement-based mental health care. Any new measurement tool would have to overcome these barriers by creating clear value for both the person with lived experience and the clinician.</li>\n<li><strong>There is value in combining subjective and objective data</strong>. People with lived experience and clinicians both welcomed the introduction of objective metrics, but not as a replacement for subjective assessment and asking people about their experience and feelings. The combination of subjective and objective metrics was seen as especially powerful. Objective metrics might validate the subjective experience; or if the two diverge, that in itself is an interesting insight which provides the starting point for a conversation.</li>\n<li><strong>There are multiple use cases for new measurement technology.</strong> Our initial hypothesis was that clinicians might use a “brainwave test” as a diagnostic aid. However, this concept got a lukewarm reception. Mental health experts such as psychiatrists and clinical psychologists felt confident in their ability to diagnose via clinical interview. Primary care physicians thought an EEG test could be useful, but only if it was conducted by a medical assistant before their consultation with the patient, similar to a blood pressure test. Counsellors and social workers don’t do diagnosis in their practice, so it was irrelevant to them. Some people with lived experience did not like the idea of being labelled as depressed by a machine. By contrast, there was a notably strong interest in using technology as a tool for ongoing monitoring — capturing changes in mental health state over time — to learn what happens between visits. Many clinicians asked if they could send the EEG system home so their patients and clients could repeat the test on their own. They were also very interested in EEG’s potential predictive qualities, e.g. predicting who is likely to get more depressed in future. More research is needed to determine how a tool such as EEG would be best deployed in clinical and counseling settings, including how it could be combined with other measurement technologies such as digital phenotyping.</li>\n</ol>\n</blockquote>\n<p>X is making Amber&#8217;s hardware and software open-source on <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/github\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"github\">GitHub, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and is also issuing a &#8220;patent pledge&#8221; that ensures X will not bring any legal action against users of the EEG patents related to Amber through use of the open-sourced material.</p>\n<p>It&#8217;s unclear (though unlikely) that this would have been the result had Amber succeeded at finding a single biomarker for depression, but perhaps in the hands of the broader community, the work the team did on rendering EEG more accessible beyond specialized testing facilities will lead to other interesting discoveries.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=SuMNaUgMEeQ:R1KImLNiMPY:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/SuMNaUgMEeQ\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 02 Nov 2020 20:23:08 +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI","linkMd5":"ce8411f09376f499e05c64e6e50815ea","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn22@2020_6/2020/11/03/05-31-20-196_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","destWidth":59,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":990,"destBytes":324,"author":"Darrell Etherington","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn22@2020_6/2020/11/03/05-31-20-196_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn96@2020_5/2020/11/03/05-31-35-908_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn52@2020_4/2020/11/03/05-31-34-882_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=SuMNaUgMEeQ:R1KImLNiMPY:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn49@2020_1/2020/11/03/05-31-35-922_2ff6f72c94950e16.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=SuMNaUgMEeQ:R1KImLNiMPY:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn68@2020_4/2020/11/03/05-31-34-808_f92ade59b71898ab.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn35@2020_5/2020/11/03/05-31-35-960_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/SuMNaUgMEeQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn50@2020_5/2020/11/03/05-31-35-993_11c0c0d548d84855.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1604381479576},{"createdTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:19","updatedTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:19","title":"Spotify will now allow artists and labels to promote tracks in your recommendations","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2068739","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/spotify\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"spotify\">Spotify <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> <a href=\"https://newsroom.spotify.com/2020-11-02/amplifying-artist-input-in-your-personalized-recommendations/\">announced</a> today it will begin to test a new service that gives artists more of a say in how their music is discovered on the Spotify platform. At launch, the service will allow artists and labels to identify music that&#8217;s a priority to them, and Spotify will then add a signal to help the music get surfaced by its personalization algorithms.</p>\n<p>While the new service is not a paid promotion and requires no upfront budget on artists&#8217; or labels&#8217; part, Spotify says that the artists, labels and rights holders will agree to be paid a &#8220;promotional recording royalty rate&#8221; for streams where the company provides the service. Streams that come from any other place in the app would not be impacted, however.</p>\n<p>At launch, the promotional rate will apply only in select areas of Spotify&#8217;s app, including Spotify Radio and Autoplay. Promoted tracks won&#8217;t appear on other playlists, either algorithmic or editorial &#8212; though Spotify isn&#8217;t ruling out expansion to these areas in the future.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>&#8220;We wanted to make the tools accessible and available to artists of any size, at any phase in their career,&#8221; explains Spotify Product Marketing Lead Charleton Lamb in describing the new service. That&#8217;s why the company won&#8217;t require an upfront payment from artists and labels, he says.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We were looking for a model that was acceptable, more democratic and fair&#8230;The model is going to allow even really small artists to access promotions at the same terms of the biggest labels,&#8221; Lamb adds.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2068831\" style=\"width: 638px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2068831\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2068831\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Spotify_Personalized-Recommendations.png?w=628\" alt=\"\" width=\"628\" height=\"680\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Spotify_Personalized-Recommendations.png 1200w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Spotify_Personalized-Recommendations.png?resize=138,150 138w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Spotify_Personalized-Recommendations.png?resize=277,300 277w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Spotify_Personalized-Recommendations.png?resize=768,832 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Spotify_Personalized-Recommendations.png?resize=628,680 628w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Spotify_Personalized-Recommendations.png?resize=46,50 46w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 628px) 100vw, 628px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2068831\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits: </strong>Spotify</p></div></p>\n<p>The idea is that if a track does well due to the promotion, the rights holders would see an overall positive ROI as the music becomes more popular and sees increased plays outside of the areas where the lower, promotional rate applies. Artists can also turn off the promotions at any time if the tool is not having a positive financial benefit.</p>\n<p>Spotify isn&#8217;t detailing the extent of the royalty rate change for promotions, saying that it may be adjusted as a result of the test.</p>\n<p>The company also stresses it will take listener interest and enjoyment into consideration with this change. Spotify says if the music performs well, it will continue to promote it. But if it doesn&#8217;t, it will be pulled back.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We won’t guarantee placement to labels or artists, and we only ever recommend music we think listeners will want to hear,&#8221; Spotify notes, in <a href=\"https://newsroom.spotify.com/2020-11-02/amplifying-artist-input-in-your-personalized-recommendations/\">its public announcement.</a></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"ljaO6hsgkK\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/29/spotify-ceo-says-company-will-further-expand-price-increases/\">Spotify CEO says company will &#8216;further expand price increases&#8217;</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Spotify CEO says company will &#8216;further expand price increases&#8217;&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/29/spotify-ceo-says-company-will-further-expand-price-increases/embed/#?secret=ljaO6hsgkK\" data-secret=\"ljaO6hsgkK\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Lamb clarifies this means users may hear a promoted track if they already listen to that genre or artist, but also if there are other signals that indicate a user may be receptive to the music. For example, users could come across the promoted track if the music was acoustically similar to what they already listen to. It could also be placed in front of the user if they listen to similar artists, or if people who have similar listening habits also listen to that music.</p>\n<p>The reverse will also be true. If those who share a user&#8217;s listening habits are negatively responding to a promoted track &#8212; perhaps by skipping it in a session or choosing to stream less frequently from Radio, for instance &#8212; the music could be pulled back.</p>\n<p>&#8220;If any kind of recommendation was causing a listener to respond negatively or show less interest in radio systems, then we would adjust how we&#8217;re recommending,&#8221; Lamb says.</p>\n<p>This user feedback loop can quickly impact the extent with which the track is promoted, he also notes, as the recommendation pools for listeners are updated every 24 hours.</p>\n<p>There is currently no limit to how many tracks that an artist or label can promote at once, nor any limit on the time frame of the promotion.</p>\n<p>While artists can promote tracks of any recency, Spotify believes the largest focus for this tool would be on catalog music. For example, if the artist is looking to celebrate an album anniversary or take advantage of a &#8220;cultural moment.&#8221;</p>\n<p>In other words, if an artist sees sudden viral success for an older track, this service could help. That&#8217;s something that&#8217;s happening with much more frequency these days, thanks to <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/tiktok\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"tiktok\">TikTok, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> which is helping surface older tunes when they get featured as the background track in viral videos.</p>\n<p>For example, when TikTok user Nathan Apodaca &#8212; better known as <a href=\"https://www.tiktok.com/@420doggface208?lang=en\">@420doggface208</a> &#8212; recorded a video of himself skateboarding and drinking Ocean Spray&#8217;s Cran-Raspberry juice to Fleetwood Mac&#8217;s &#8220;Dreams,&#8221; the 1977 classic <a href=\"https://www.npr.org/2020/10/11/922554253/tiktok-sensation-meet-the-idaho-potato-worker-who-sent-fleetwood-mac-sales-soari\">found itself back on the top charts.</a></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"tiktok-embed\" cite=\"https://www.tiktok.com/@420doggface208/video/6876424179084709126\" data-video-id=\"6876424179084709126\" style=\"max-width: 605px;min-width: 325px;\" >\n<section> <a target=\"_blank\" title=\"@420doggface208\" href=\"https://www.tiktok.com/@420doggface208\">@420doggface208</a> </p>\n<p>Morning vibe <a title=\"420souljahz\" href=\"https://www.tiktok.com/music/Dreams-2004-Remaster-6844610572080794373\">♬ Dreams (2004 Remaster) &#8211; Fleetwood Mac</a> </section>\n</blockquote>\n<p> <script async src=\"https://www.tiktok.com/embed.js\"></script></div>\n<p><a href=\"https://newsroom.tiktok.com/en-us/doggface-gives-the-world-a-smile-with-juice-a-skateboard-and-all-the-vibes\">TikTok said</a> that from the video&#8217;s release on September 25th to mid-October, the average daily uses of &#8220;Dreams&#8221; in TikTok videos climbed 1,380%, which then translated to a 374% jump in sales and an 89% jump in streams. This allowed the song to re-enter the Billboard Hot 100 at No. 21 after a 43-year absence. It also climbed to the Top Ten of Spotify’s Global and U.S. charts and hit No. 1 on Apple Music.</p>\n<p>That&#8217;s precisely the type of &#8220;cultural moment&#8221; Spotify now aims to profit from.</p>\n<p>Though the service is not exactly a &#8220;pay for play&#8221; model, it is a financially tied service for music promotion that effectively allows Spotify to make more money when streams are &#8220;promoted&#8221; with the new tool.</p>\n<p>Spotify has been inching its way into the pay for play market for years. In 2019,<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/10/24/spotify-now-lets-artists-buy-a-full-screen-recommendation-promoting-their-new-album/\"> the company introduced</a> a new feature that allows artists to buy a full-screen recommendation to promote their new album to users Spotify has identified as fans. <a href=\"https://www.rollingstone.com/pro/features/spotify-marquee-ad-cost-5000-915990/\">Rolling Stone said</a> each ad click cost 55 cents, citing internal documents.</p>\n<p>Though the feature was targeted toward users who would be more likely to welcome such a notification, it was criticized as being a new form of payola &#8212; meaning labels that had the most money to spend would get the most play.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"q6GAxnJH9x\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/14/spotify-introduces-a-new-music-and-spoken-word-format-open-to-all-creators/\">Spotify introduces a new music-and-spoken word format, open to all creators</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Spotify introduces a new music-and-spoken word format, open to all creators&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/14/spotify-introduces-a-new-music-and-spoken-word-format-open-to-all-creators/embed/#?secret=q6GAxnJH9x\" data-secret=\"q6GAxnJH9x\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>In previous years, Spotify had also been criticized <a href=\"https://www.billboard.com/articles/business/6670475/playola-promotion-streaming-services\">for allowing payola to infiltrate its playlists.</a> And the company famously <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/07/03/spotify-users-push-back-at-the-over-the-top-drake-promotion/\">angered its users in 2018 with an over-the-top Drake album promotion</a> that placed the album and Drake&#8217;s image in sections of the app like Browse and Playlists, and used Drake&#8217;s image on playlists that didn&#8217;t even contain his music &#8212; like those featuring dance hits, pop and more.</p>\n<p>This new service, on the other hand, aims to counter some of the issues with past promotions, as it would favor pushing tracks to already receptive users &#8212; and it would do so in a less over-the-top way than with pop-up ads or overboard global promotions.</p>\n<p>Spotify has tested the technology before now with a small number of partners, but says it will now begin to roll out the test and the promoted rate in the U.S.</p>\n<p>During the test period, it will work with a small handful of labels, including both indies and majors, to gain a variety of feedback. Spotify says the feature will expand globally in the future.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=wdypgvVUB-U:EKj2ntJOp7E:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Spotify_Personalized-Recommendations.png?w=628","linkMd5":"365c308e14374f8bff1350b8226bae62","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn10@2020_2/2020/11/03/05-31-20-079_c58c6ea513293462.webp","destWidth":628,"destHeight":680,"sourceBytes":180592,"destBytes":180592,"author":"Sarah Perez","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Spotify_Personalized-Recommendations.png?w=628":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn10@2020_2/2020/11/03/05-31-20-079_c58c6ea513293462.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn22@2020_6/2020/11/03/05-31-20-196_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn96@2020_5/2020/11/03/05-31-35-908_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn52@2020_4/2020/11/03/05-31-34-882_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=wdypgvVUB-U:EKj2ntJOp7E:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn27@2020_6/2020/11/03/05-31-34-764_b7f4e192d6725436.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=wdypgvVUB-U:EKj2ntJOp7E:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn3@2020_1/2020/11/03/05-31-35-903_86e327b40d395b0e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn35@2020_5/2020/11/03/05-31-35-960_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/wdypgvVUB-U":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn23@2020_2/2020/11/03/05-31-34-788_4809d11baac3131e.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1604381479576},{"createdTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:19","updatedTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:19","title":"What social networks have learned since the 2016 election","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2068738","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">On the eve on the 2020 U.S. election, tensions are running high.</p>\n<p>The good news? 2020 isn&#8217;t 2016. Social networks are way better prepared to handle a wide array of complex, dangerous or otherwise ambiguous Election Day scenarios.</p>\n<p>The bad news: 2020 is its own beast, one that&#8217;s unleashed a nightmare health scenario on a divided nation that&#8217;s even more susceptible now to misinformation, hyper-partisanship and dangerous ideas moving from the fringe to the center than it was four years ago.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The U.S. was caught off guard by foreign interference in the 2016 election, but shocking a nation that&#8217;s spent the last eight months expecting a convergence of worst-case scenarios won&#8217;t be so easy.</p>\n<p>Social platforms have braced for the 2020 election in a way they didn&#8217;t in 2016. Here&#8217;s what they&#8217;re worried about and the critical lessons from the last four years that they&#8217;ll bring to bear.</p>\n<h2>Contested election results</h2>\n<p>President Trump has repeatedly signaled that he won&#8217;t accept the results of the election in the case that he loses — a shocking threat that could imperil American democracy, but one social platforms have been tracking closely. Trump&#8217;s erratic, often rule-bending behavior on social networks in recent months has served as a kind of stress test, allowing those platforms to game out different scenarios for the election.</p>\n<p><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/facebook\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"facebook\">Facebook <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> and Twitter in particular have laid out detailed plans about what happens if the results of the election aren&#8217;t immediately clear or if a candidate refuses to accept official results once they&#8217;re tallied.</p>\n<p>On election night, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/07/facebook-poll-watching-trump-election-political-ads/\">Facebook will pin a message</a> to the top of both Facebook and Instagram telling users that vote counting is still underway. When authoritative results are in, Facebook will change those messages to reflect the official results. Importantly, U.S. election results might not be clear on election night or for some days afterward, a potential outcome for which Facebook and other social networks are bracing.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2068942\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2068942\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2068942\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/facebook-election-message.jpeg?w=680\" alt=\"Facebook election message\" width=\"680\" height=\"623\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/facebook-election-message.jpeg 890w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/facebook-election-message.jpeg?resize=150,138 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/facebook-election-message.jpeg?resize=300,275 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/facebook-election-message.jpeg?resize=768,704 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/facebook-election-message.jpeg?resize=680,623 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/facebook-election-message.jpeg?resize=50,46 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2068942\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Image via Facebook</p></div></p>\n<p>If a candidate declared victory prematurely, Facebook doesn&#8217;t say it will remove those claims, but it will pair them with its message that there&#8217;s no official result and voting is still underway.</p>\n<p><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/twitter\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"twitter\">Twitter <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/10/twitter-contested-election-misinformation-policy-trump/\">released its plans</a> for handling election results two months ago, explaining that it will either remove or attach a warning label to premature claims of victory before authoritative election results are in. The company also explicitly stated that it will act against any tweets &#8220;inciting unlawful conduct to prevent a peaceful transfer of power or orderly succession,&#8221; a shocking rule to have to articulate, but a necessary one in 2020.</p>\n<p>On Monday, Twitter <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/02/twitter-explains-how-it-will-handle-misleading-tweets-about-the-us-election-results/\">elaborated on its policy</a>, saying that it would focus on labeling misleading tweets about the presidential election and other contested races. The company released a sample image of a label it would append, showing a warning stating that &#8220;this tweet is sharing inaccurate information.&#8221;</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">We may label Tweets, starting on election night, that make claims about election results before they’re officially called.</p>\n<p>We’ll be prioritizing the presidential election and other highly contested races where there may be significant issues with misleading information. <a href=\"https://t.co/BExhZdVMnB\">pic.twitter.com/BExhZdVMnB</a></p>\n<p>&#8212; Twitter Support (@TwitterSupport) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/TwitterSupport/status/1323265831904677889?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">November 2, 2020</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></div>\n<p>Last week, the company also began <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/26/twitter-notification-voting-by-mail-delayed-election-results/\">showing users large misinformation warnings</a> at the top of their feeds. The messages told users that they &#8220;might encounter misleading information&#8221; about mail-in voting and also cautioned them that election results may not be immediately known.</p>\n<p>According to Twitter, users who try to share tweets with misleading election-related misinformation will see a pop-up pointing them to vetted information and forcing them to click through a warning before sharing. Twitter also says it will act on any &#8220;disputed claims&#8221; that might cast doubt on voting, including &#8220;unverified information about election rigging, ballot tampering, vote tallying, or certification of election results.&#8221;</p>\n<p>One other major change that many users probably already noticed is <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/09/twitter-retweet-changes-quote-tweet-election-misinformation/\">Twitter&#8217;s decision to disable retweets</a>. Users can still retweet by clicking through a pop-up page, but Twitter made the change to encourage people to quote retweet instead. The effort to slow down the spread of misinformation was striking, and Twitter said it will stay in place through the end of election week, at least.</p>\n<p>YouTube didn&#8217;t go into similar detail about its decision making, but the <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2020/10/27/youtube-election-day-warning-label-results-may-not-be-final-.html\">company previously said</a> it will put an &#8220;informational&#8221; label on search results related to the election and below election-related videos. The label warns users that &#8220;results may not be final&#8221; and points them to the company&#8217;s election info hub.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"UtJhbzHgKd\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/24/youtube-voting-misinformation-election/\">YouTube will add vetted info about mail-in voting to counter election misinformation</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;YouTube will add vetted info about mail-in voting to counter election misinformation&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/24/youtube-voting-misinformation-election/embed/#?secret=UtJhbzHgKd\" data-secret=\"UtJhbzHgKd\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<h2>Foreign disinformation</h2>\n<p>This is one area where social networks have made big strides. After Russian disinformation <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/05/10/russian-facebook-ads-house-intelligence-full-list/\">took root on social platforms four years ago</a>, those companies now coordinate with one another and the government about the threats they’re seeing.</p>\n<p>In the aftermath of 2016, Facebook eventually woke up to the idea that its platform could be leveraged to scale social ills like hate and misinformation. Its scorecard is uneven, but its actions against foreign disinformation have been <a href=\"https://about.fb.com/news/tag/coordinated-inauthentic-behavior/\">robust</a>, reducing that threat considerably.</p>\n<p>A repeat of the same concerns from 2016 is unlikely. Facebook made aggressive efforts to find foreign coordinated disinformation campaigns across its platforms, and it publishes what it finds regularly and with little delay. But in 2020, the biggest concerns are coming from within the country — not without.</p>\n<p>Most foreign information operations have been small so far, failing to gain much traction. Last month, Facebook removed <a href=\"https://about.fb.com/news/2020/10/removing-coordinated-inauthentic-behavior-mexico-iran-myanmar/\">a network of fake accounts</a> connected to Iran. The operation was small and failed to generate much traction, but it shows that U.S. adversaries are still interested in trying out the tactic.</p>\n<h2>Misleading political ads</h2>\n<p>To address concerns around election misinformation in ads, Facebook opted for a temporary political ad blackout, starting at 12 a.m. PT on November 4 and continuing until the company deems it safe to toggle them back on. Facebook hasn&#8217;t accepted any new political ads <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/03/facebook-to-block-new-political-ads-1-week-before-nov-3-adds-more-tools-and-rules-for-fair-elections/\">since October 27</a> and previously said it won&#8217;t accept any ads that <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/01/facebook-election-ad-ban-delegitimize-election-results/\">delegitimize the results</a> of the election. Google will also pause election-related ads after polls close Tuesday.</p>\n<p>Facebook has made a number of big changes to political ads since 2016, when <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/05/10/russian-facebook-ads-house-intelligence-full-list/\">Russia bought Facebook ads</a> to meddle with U.S. politics. Political ads on the platform are subject to more scrutiny and much more transparency now and <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/ads/library/\">Facebook&#8217;s ad library</a> emerged as an exemplary tool that allows anyone to see what ads have been published, who bought them and how much they spent.</p>\n<p>Unlike Facebook, Twitter&#8217;s way of dealing with political advertising was <a href=\"https://www.thedailybeast.com/jack-dorsey-twitter-will-no-longer-accept-political-and-issue-ads\">cutting it off entirely</a>. The company announced the change a year ago and hasn&#8217;t looked back since. TikTok also opted to <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/10/03/tiktok-explains-its-ban-on-political-advertising/\">disallow political ads</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">We’ve made the decision to stop all political advertising on Twitter globally. We believe political message reach should be earned, not bought. Why? A few reasons…<img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/13.0.0/72x72/1f9f5.png\" alt=\"🧵\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /></p>\n<p>&#8212; jack (@jack) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/jack/status/1189634360472829952?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">October 30, 2019</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></div>\n<h2>Political violence</h2>\n<p>Politically motivated violence is a big worry this week in the U.S. — a concern that shows just how tense the situation has grown under four years of Trump. Leading into Tuesday, the president has repeatedly made <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/05/26/twitter-trump-labels-fact-checking-tweet/\">false claims of voter fraud</a> and encouraged his followers to engage in voter intimidation, a threat Facebook was clued into enough that it made a policy <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/07/facebook-poll-watching-trump-election-political-ads/\">prohibiting &#8220;militarized&#8221; language</a> around poll watching.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"XQsntpfpXu\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/07/facebook-poll-watching-trump-election-political-ads/\">Facebook: Trump can&#8217;t recruit &#8216;army&#8217; of poll watchers under new voter intimidation rules</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Facebook: Trump can&#8217;t recruit &#8216;army&#8217; of poll watchers under new voter intimidation rules&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/07/facebook-poll-watching-trump-election-political-ads/embed/#?secret=XQsntpfpXu\" data-secret=\"XQsntpfpXu\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Facebook made a number of other meaningful recent changes, like <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/06/facebook-qanon-ban/\">banning the dangerous pro-Trump conspiracy theory QAnon</a> and <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/08/gretchen-whitmer-kidnapping-plot-facebook-groups-militias-fbi/\">militias that use the platform to organize</a>, though those efforts have come very late in the game.</p>\n<p>Facebook was <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/06/01/facebook-employees-stage-virtual-walkout-in-protest-of-companys-stance-on-trump-posts/\">widely criticized for its inaction</a> around a Trump post warning &#8220;when the looting starts, the shooting starts&#8221; during racial justice protests earlier this year, but its recent posture suggests similar posts might be taken more seriously now. We&#8217;ll be watching how Facebook handles emerging threats of violence this week.</p>\n<p>Its recent decisive moves against extremism are important, but the platform has long incubated groups that use the company&#8217;s networking and event tools to come together for potential real-world violence. Even if they aren&#8217;t allowed on the platform any longer, many of those groups got organized and then moved their networks onto alternative social networks and private channels. Still, making it more difficult to organize violence on mainstream social networks is a big step in the right direction.</p>\n<p>Twitter also addressed the potential threat of election-related violence in advance, noting that it may add warnings or require users to remove any tweets &#8220;inciting interference with the election&#8221; or encouraging violence.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"cWL86Xvi79\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/06/facebook-qanon-ban/\">Facebook says it will ban QAnon across its platforms</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Facebook says it will ban QAnon across its platforms&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/06/facebook-qanon-ban/embed/#?secret=cWL86Xvi79\" data-secret=\"cWL86Xvi79\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<h2>Platform policy shifts in 2020</h2>\n<p>Facebook is the biggest online arena where U.S. political life plays out. While a similar number of Americans watch videos on YouTube, Facebook is where they go to duke it out over candidates, share news stories (some legitimate, some not) and generally express themselves politically. It&#8217;s a tinderbox in normal times — and 2020 is far from normal.</p>\n<p>While Facebook acted against foreign threats quickly after 2016, the company dragged its feet on platform changes that could be perceived as politically motivated — a hesitation that backfired by incubating dangerous extremists and allowing many kinds of misinformation, particularly on the far-right, to survive and thrive.</p>\n<p>In spite of Facebook&#8217;s lingering <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/technology/2020/11/01/facebook-election-misinformation/\">misguided political fears</a>, there are reasons to be hopeful that the company might avert election-related catastrophes.</p>\n<p>Whether it was inspired by the threat of a contested election, federal antitrust action or a possible Biden presidency, Facebook has signaled a shift to more thoughtful moderation with a flurry of recent policy enforcement decisions. An accompanying flurry of election-focused podcast and television ads suggests Facebook is worried about public perception too — and it should be.</p>\n<p>Twitter&#8217;s plan for the election has been well-communicated and detailed. In 2020, the company treats its policy decisions with more transparency, communicates them in real time and isn&#8217;t afraid to admit to mistakes. The relatively small social network plays an outsized role in publishing political content that&#8217;s amplified elsewhere, so the choices it makes are critical for countering misinformation and extremism.</p>\n<p>The companies that host and amplify online political conversation have learned some major lessons since 2016 — mostly the hard way. Let&#8217;s just hope it was enough to help them guide their roiling platforms through one of the most fraught moments in modern U.S. history.</p>\n<p><a
