13:31:19","updatedTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:19","title":"Booming edtech M&A activity brings consolidation to a fragmented sector","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2068705","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">As the COVID-19 pandemic continues to force teachers, students and parents to adopt new technologies, edtech’s total addressable market has massively grown in the last several months. The shift has urged venture capitalists to pour money into the sector accordingly, ushering a number of startups into the unicorn club.</p>\n<p>But maturation doesn’t just mean bigger checks and high-flying unicorns &#8212; it also brings exits.</p>\n<p>Edtech M&#38;A activity is buzzier than usual: In the last week, <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/coursehero\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"coursehero\">Course Hero, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> a startup that sells Netflix-like subscriptions to students looking for learning and teaching content, bought <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/symbolab\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"symbolab\">Symbolab, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/27/course-hero-symbolab-makes-a-rare-edtech-acquisition/?tpcc=ECTW2020\">an artificial intelligence-powered calculator</a>. Saga Education, a tutoring nonprofit backed by Comcast, the Bill &#38; Melinda Gates Foundation and others, acquired math software platform Woot Math. We also saw PowerSchool, which sells a suite of software services to manage schools, scoop up Hoonuit, a data management and analytics tool for educators. Finally, K-12 curriculum company Discovery Education bought K-5 science and stem curriculum upstart Mystery Science.</p>\n<p>It’s a lot of news in a short period of time. Luckily, these consolidations offer some directional guidance regarding where some edtech businesses think the future of their industry is headed.</p>\n<h2>Smart content as a competitive advantage</h2>\n<p>Content, to an extent, is commoditized. If you can find a free tutorial on Youtube or <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/khan-academy\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"khan-academy\">Khan Academy, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> buy a subscription to an edtech platform that offers the same solution? The commodification of education is good for end-users and is often why startups have a freemium model as a customer acquisition strategy. To convert free users into paying subscribers, edtech startups need to offer differentiated and targeted content.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"vXgpIr9t5s\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/13/edtech-exits-show-a-need-for-better-plumbing/\">Edtech exits show a need for better plumbing</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Edtech exits show a need for better plumbing&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/13/edtech-exits-show-a-need-for-better-plumbing/embed/#?secret=vXgpIr9t5s\" data-secret=\"vXgpIr9t5s\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>The Course Hero and Mystery Science deals show us that edtech businesses are hungry for personalized, targeted content. Course Hero’s acquisition of Symbolab was essentially a deal for more than a decade&#8217;s worth of data that captured which math questions students found hardest.</p>\n<p>Symbolab is a math calculator that is set to answer over 1 billion questions this year. With each answer, Symbolab adds information to its algorithm regarding students&#8217; most common pain points and confusion. Course Hero, in contrast, is a broader service that focuses on Q&#38;A from a variety of subjects. CEO <a href=\"https://twitter.com/atgrauer?lang=en\">Andrew Grauer</a> says Symbolab’s algorithm isn’t something that Course Hero, which has been operating since 2006, can drum up overnight. That’s precisely why he “decided to buy, instead of build.”</p>\n<p>“It made a lot of sense to move fast enough so it wouldn&#8217;t take up multiple years to get this technology,” Grauer said. The deal was made as big companies get in the Q&#38;A game too, he noted. <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/google\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"google\">Google <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> acquired homework helper app Socratic in 2019 and <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/microsoft\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"microsoft\">Microsoft <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> built Microsoft Solver in the same year.</p>\n<p>Discovery Education, a curriculum provider for K-12 classrooms, acquired San Francisco-based K-5 STEM curriculum provider, Mystery Science. Discovery Education has launched a series of other products focused on science education, including Discovery Education Experience, the Science Techbook series and STEM Connect.  However, Mystery Science is largely focused on offering a creative digital solution to science education. The programming, a mix of videos, prompts and projects, cover a range of questions such as, “Where do rivers flow?” and “Could a volcano pop up where you live?” for young students.</p>\n<p>Mystery Science CEO and founder Keith Schact explained how his product focuses on kids and educators, while Discovery Education focuses on educators and districts, making the deal feel like a &#8220;natural marriage.&#8221; Even as edtech goes directly to consumers, Schact remains bullish on the role that institutions play in true adoption of technology.</p>\n<p>&#8220;You can go straight to teachers and get a certain market share,&#8221; he said. &#8220;But the institutions still do have a big role.&#8221; The founder likened the dynamic to the state of media: With the rise of blogs, you can publish directly and reach an engaged audience, but writers who want a bigger positioning tend to join larger platforms to grow their overall reach. Edtech is the same, in that some startups need an official sign-off from schools before they can reach venture-scale returns.</p>\n<p>According to a source familiar with the transaction, Mystery Science was sold for $175 million after only raising $4 million in venture financing.</p>\n<h2>Using data management and analytics to improve student outcomes<div id=\"speakable-summary\">Financial guidance company <a href=\"http://www.nerdwallet.com\">NerdWallet</a> announced at the end of last week that it has acquired <a href=\"http://www.fundera.com\">Fundera</a>. New York City-based <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/fundera\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"fundera\">Fundera <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> was co-founded in 2013 by Jared Hecht, who previously co-founded GroupMe. It <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2015/09/17/fundera-picks-up-11-5-million-in-series-b-funding/\">created a marketplace where small businesses could find loans</a>, subsequently expanding into other areas like legal services, while also (like NerdWallet) offering free financial content.</p>\n<p>&#8220;It can be the wild wild west out there for small business owners,&#8221; Hecht said in a statement. &#8220;Finding the financial products and the guidance needed to start, grow and fund their businesses can be very challenging, and most small business owners don&#8217;t have a resource or partner to support them along their journey. Bringing transparency to this process and educating, empowering and advocating for business owners is so similar to what we see <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/nerdwallet\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"nerdwallet\">NerdWallet <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> doing in the consumer space.&#8221;</p>\n<p>And of course, small businesses may be in particularly dire need of assistance now, given the impact of the pandemic.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>According to <a href=\"https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/nerdwallet-acquires-fundera-the-go-to-small-business-resource-301163831.html\">the announcement</a>, Fundera will operate as a subsidiary of NerdWallet, with the entire team making the transition. The goal is to help NerdWallet expand into the small- and medium-business market with both content and actual financing.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Although we offer free tools and content, we&#8217;ve never been able to fully support small business owners — that changes today,&#8221; said NerdWallet co-founder and CEO Tim Chen. &#8220;Fundera has been one of our partners for several years and their deep understanding of the SMB market, the long-standing, trusted relationships they&#8217;ve built with both lenders and business owners, and their commitment to putting the needs of small business owners first is really unique and impressive.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The financial terms of the acquisition were not disclosed. Fundera had raised $18.9 million in funding from investors including QED Investors, Khosla Ventures, First Round Capital and Susquehanna Growth Equity, <a href=\"https://www.crunchbase.com/organization/fundera\">according to Crunchbase</a>.</p>\n<p>This is NerdWallet&#8217;s second acquisition of 2020, having <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/27/nerdwallet-acquires-uks-know-your-money-as-it-expands-outside-the-us/\">previously acquired U.K.-based Know Your Money</a>. 13:31:19","updatedTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:19","title":"Walmart reportedly ends contract with inventory robotics startup Bossa Nova","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2068995","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Robotics and automation startups have seen a strong uptick in interest over the course of the pandemic. And it’s easy to see which companies have a newfound interest in automating their workforce amid a seemingly endless virus-driven shutdown. But <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/walmart\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"walmart\">Walmart, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> which has long promised to take an increasing focus on such technology, has reportedly pulled the plug on one of its highest-profile partnerships.</p>\n<p>The mega-retailer has ended a contract with <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/bossa-nova-robotics-inc\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"bossa-nova-robotics-inc\">Bossa Nova Robotics, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> according to new reporting from <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/walmart-shelves-plan-to-have-robots-scan-shelves-11604345341?mod=e2fb&#38;fbclid=IwAR0cNEqLBvbRxHyJNi4RTFmrwyKQrBYP4FQHF4lridWWJHEyPZVhI2yLNhY\">The Wall Street Journal</a>. Walmart had announced in January that it would bring the Bay Area-based startup’s inventory-scanning robots to an additional 650 locations, bringing the total up to 1,000. The move has resulted in layoffs of around 50% at the Carnegie Mellon spin-off, per the WSJ report. It’s a huge hit at a time when such technologies should be thriving.</p>\n<p>Bossa Nova co-founder Sarjoun Skaff didn&#8217;t confirm nor deny the WSJ report, instead issuing a no comment. He did, however, weigh in on the COVID-19 pandemic and its affect on the company, seeming to confirm that some layoffs had indeed occurred.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>&#8220;I cannot comment on Walmart, however, the pandemic has forced us to streamline our operations and focus on our core technologies,&#8221; Skaff said. &#8220;We have made stunning advances in AI and robotics. Our retail AI is the industry&#8217;s best and works as well on robots as with fixed cameras, and our hardware, autonomy and operations excelled in more than 500 of the world&#8217;s most challenging stores. With the board&#8217;s full support, we continue deploying this technology with our partners in retail and in other fields.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The tumult at Bossa Nova has stretched beyond layoffs. Skaff, who was CTO, took over the CEO spot in October when Stuart Pann left the position after less than nine months. Bossa Nova&#8217;s deal with Walmart was a major break for the startup, which began life in 2005 as a robotic toymaker before pivoting into something more serious. The startup&#8217;s relationship with Walmart dates back to 2017, when the chain ordered 50 robots.  Walmart&#8217;s massive order earlier was a major endorsement of Bossa Nova&#8217;s technology.</p>\n<p>Such a change of heart would no doubt have a profound effect on the company.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"kt9OHGOuoe\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/21/sams-club-will-deploy-autonomous-floor-scrubbing-robots-in-all-of-its-u-s-locations/\">Sam’s Club will deploy autonomous floor-scrubbing robots in all of its US locations</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Sam’s Club will deploy autonomous floor-scrubbing robots in all of its US locations&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/21/sams-club-will-deploy-autonomous-floor-scrubbing-robots-in-all-of-its-u-s-locations/embed/#?secret=kt9OHGOuoe\" data-secret=\"kt9OHGOuoe\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Walmart apparently just wasn’t getting enough out of the deal. Bossa Nova’s robots had made their way into around 500 stores by the time the deal ended — around half of the initial proposed number. As COVID-19 has pushed more orders online, Walmart began exploring ways to use human workers to perform inventory while grabbing product for online fulfillment. Walmart&#8217;s operations, as well as those at other major retailers, will continue to evolve as brick-and-mortar locations reopen and customers shows signs of interest to return to the in-person shopping experience. The volatility of the pandemic still doesn&#8217;t lessen the sting or impact that Walmart&#8217;s abrupt reversal will have on Bossa Nova and its hopes for a rebound.</p>\n<p>Meanwhile, Walmart’s robotic experiments aren’t over. The company’s Sam’s Club subsidiary recently announced it would bring Tennant’s floor scrubbing robots to all of its 599 stores. Interestingly, the company is also exploring ways for these machines to double up and perform in-store inventory checks; it&#8217;s not clear if these will be used only in Sam&#8217;s Club locations or extend to Walmart stores as well.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"VGUokA3o6d\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/01/13/bossa-novas-inventory-robots-are-rolling-out-in-1000-walmart-stores/\">Bossa Nova’s inventory robots are rolling out in 1,000 Walmart stores</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Bossa Nova’s inventory robots are rolling out in 1,000 Walmart shipments","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2068577","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Indonesia’s logistics industry is <a href=\"http://www.gbgindonesia.com/en/services/article/2013/indonesia_s_logistics_sector.php\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">very fragmented</a>, with several large providers operating alongside thousands of smaller companies. This means shippers often have to work with a variety of carriers, driving up costs and making supply chains harder to manage. <a href=\"https://logisly.com/\">Logisly</a>, a Jakarta-based startup that describes itself as a &#8220;B2B tech-enabled logistics platform,&#8221; announced today it has raised $6 million in Series A funding to help streamline logistics in Indonesia. The round was led by Monk’s Hill Ventures.</p>\n<p>This brings the total <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/logisly\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"logisly\">Logisly <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> has raised since it was founded last year to $7 million. Its platform digitizes the process of ordering, managing and tracking trucks. First, it verifies carriers before adding them to Logisly&#8217;s platform. Then it connects clients to trucking providers, using an algorithm to aggregate supply and demand. This means companies that need to ship goods can find trucks more quickly, while carriers can reduce the number of unused space on their trucks.</p>\n<p>Co-founder and chief executive officer Roolin Njotosetiadi told TechCrunch that about &#8220;40% of trucks are utilized in Indonesia, and the rest are either sitting idle or coming back from their hauls empty handed. All of these result in high logistics costs and late deliveries.&#8221;</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>She added that Logisly is &#8220;laser focused on having the largest trucking network in Indonesia, providing 100% availability of cost-efficient and reliable trucks.&#8221;</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"nbRBkAQBYI\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/09/18/shipper-a-platform-for-e-commerce-logistics-in-indonesia-raises-5-million/\">Shipper, a platform for e-commerce logistics in Indonesia, raises $5 million</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Shipper, a platform for e-commerce logistics in Indonesia, raises $5 million&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/09/18/shipper-a-platform-for-e-commerce-logistics-in-indonesia-raises-5-million/embed/#?secret=nbRBkAQBYI\" data-secret=\"nbRBkAQBYI\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Logisly now works with more than 1,000 businesses in Indonesia in sectors like e-commerce, fast-moving consumer goods (FCG), chemicals and construction. This number includes 300 corporate shippers. Logisly’s Series A will be used on growing its network of shippers and transporters (which currently covers 40,000 trucks) and on product development.</p>\n<p>The startup&#8217;s clients include some of the largest corporate shippers in Indonesia, including Unilever, Haier, Grab, Maersk and JD.ID, the Indonesian subsidiary of JD.com, one of China’s largest e-commerce companies.</p>\n<p>Other The deal was pegged at $1.5 billion.</p>\n<p>This year Llamasoft released its latest tool, <a href=\"https://llamasoft.com/platform/\">an AI-driven platform</a> for managing supply chains intelligently. This capability in particular seemed to attract Coupa&#8217;s attention, as it was looking for a supply chain application to complement its spend management capabilities.</p>\n<p>Coupa CEO and chairman <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/rob-bernshteyn\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"rob-bernshteyn\">Rob Bernshteyn <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> says when you combine that supply chain data with Coupa&#8217;s spending data, it can produce a powerful combination.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>&#8220;Llamasoft’s deep supply chain expertise and sophisticated data science and modeling capabilities, combined with the roughly $2 trillion of cumulative transactional spend data we have in Coupa, will empower businesses with the intelligence needed to pivot on a dime,&#8221; Bernshteyn said in a statement.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"hzkf2cJRgW\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/09/free-tool-helps-manufacturers-map-where-covid-19-impacts-supply-chain/\">Free tool helps manufacturers map where COVID-19 impacts supply chain</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Free tool helps manufacturers map where COVID-19 impacts supply chain&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/09/free-tool-helps-manufacturers-map-where-covid-19-impacts-supply-chain/embed/#?secret=hzkf2cJRgW\" data-secret=\"hzkf2cJRgW\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>The purchase comes at a time when companies are focusing more and more on digitizing processes across enterprise, and when supply chains can be uncertain, depending on the location of COVID hotspots at any particular time.</p>\n<p>&#8220;With demand uncertainty on one hand, and supply volatility on the other, companies are in need of supply chain technology that can help them assess alternatives and balance trade-offs to achieve desired business results. <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/llamasoft\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"llamasoft\">LLamasoft <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> provides these capabilities with an AI-powered cloud platform that empowers companies to make smarter supply chain decisions, faster,&#8221; the company wrote in a statement.</p>\n<p>Llamasoft was founded in 2002 in Ann Arbor, Michigan and has raised more than $56 million, according to Crunchbase data. Its largest raise was a $50 million Series B in 2015 led by <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/goldman-sachs\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"goldman-sachs\">Goldman Sachs <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a>.</p>\n<p>The company generated more than $100 million in revenue and has 650 big customers, including <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/boeing-7321\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"boeing-7321\">Boeing, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/dhl\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"dhl\">DHL, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> Kimberly-Clark and GM, according <a href=\"https://llamasoft.com/company/company-overview/\">to company data</a>.</p>\n<p>Coupa has been extremely acquisitive over the years, buying 17 companies, according to Crunchbase <a href=\"https://www.crunchbase.com/organization/coupa\">data</a>. This deal represents the fourth acquisition this year for the company. So far the stock market is not enamored with the acquisition; the company&#8217;s stock price is down 5.20% at publication.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote The big event will, naturally, be online-only &#8212; as it seems all big tech shows will be for the foreseeable future.</p>\n<p>The move toward virtual events amid the COVID-19 shutdown has afforded companies the ability to break these spotlight events up more than in past years. After all, simply asking reporters and analysts to tune into a livestream is a much smaller lift. As such, the company has taken advantage, with three events in quick succession. The first focused on the new Apple Watch and iPads, the second iPhones and now it seems inevitable that Apple is going to turn its attention to the Mac.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"TuwldyzI9P\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/10/new-report-outlines-potential-roadmap-for-apples-arm-based-macbooks/\">New report outlines potential roadmap for Apple’s ARM-based MacBooks</a></p></blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;New report outlines potential roadmap for Apple’s ARM-based MacBooks&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/10/new-report-outlines-potential-roadmap-for-apples-arm-based-macbooks/embed/#?secret=TuwldyzI9P\" data-secret=\"TuwldyzI9P\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>The show will likely see the long-awaited release date for macOS Big Sur, along with the unveiling of Macs built around the company&#8217;s priority ARM-based processors. Until now, however, the technology has been limited to the realm of development kits.</p>\n<p>“From the beginning, the Mac has always embraced big changes to stay at the forefront of personal computing. Today we’re announcing our transition to Apple silicon, making this a historic day for the Mac,” Tim Cook said during the announcement. “With its powerful features and industry-leading performance, Apple silicon will make the Mac stronger and more capable than ever.” It seems we&#8217;ll finally see what all of that means next week.</p>\n<p>Recent rumors have pointed to a new version of the MacBook Air set for a Q4 2020 arrival. Redesigned versions of the MacBook Pro and iMac are also reportedly in the works. The early November event is also, notably, Apple&#8217;s last chance to get products announced ahead of the holiday season. As such, it certainly seems possible we could see some other long-rumored products arrive, including its Tile-like AirTags tracking device and over-ear AirPods Studio headphones.</p>\n<p>As always, Heater","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn22@2020_6/2020/11/03/05-31-20-196_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn96@2020_5/2020/11/03/05-31-35-908_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn52@2020_4/2020/11/03/05-31-34-882_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=tHegfSh2K8g:DqrohC97N-8:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn55@2020_4/2020/11/03/05-31-34-765_4419811174caa951.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=tHegfSh2K8g:DqrohC97N-8:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn32@2020_6/2020/11/03/05-31-35-945_eb43062d71eec0bc.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn35@2020_5/2020/11/03/05-31-35-960_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/tHegfSh2K8g":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn88@2020_5/2020/11/03/05-31-34-806_96396c41b5350605.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1604381479575},{"createdTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:19","updatedTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:19","title":"Maze, a notorious ransomware group, says it’s shutting down","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2068822","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">One of the most active and notorious data-stealing ransomware groups, Maze, says it is &#8220;officially closed.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The announcement came as a waffling statement, riddled with spelling mistakes and published on its website on the dark web, which for the past year has published vast troves of stolen internal documents and files from the companies it targeted, including <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/18/cognizant-maze-ransomware/\">Cognizant</a>, cybersecurity insurance firm <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/03/26/chubb-insurance-breach-ransomware/\">Chubb</a>, pharmaceutical giant <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/27/execupharm-clop-ransomware/\">ExecuPharm</a>, Tesla and SpaceX parts supplier <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/03/01/visser-breach/\">Visser</a> and defense contractor <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/03/26/kimchuk-medical-military-ransomware/\">Kimchuk</a>.</p>\n<p>Where typical ransomware groups would infect a victim with file-encrypting malware and hold the files for a ransom, Maze gained notoriety for first exfiltrating a victim&#8217;s data and threatening to publish the stolen files unless the ransom was paid.</p>\n<p>It quickly <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/01/08/as-ransomware-gets-craftier-companies-must-start-thinking-creatively/\">became the preferred tactic</a> of ransomware groups, which set up websites — often on the dark web — to leak the files it stole if the victim refused to pay up.</p>\n<p>Maze initially used exploit kits and spam campaigns to infect its victims, but later began using known security vulnerabilities to specifically target big-name companies. Maze was <a href=\"https://www.zdnet.com/article/ransomware-gang-publishes-tens-of-gbs-of-internal-data-from-lg-and-xerox/\">known to use</a> vulnerable virtual private network (VPN) and remote desktop (RDP) servers to launch targeted attacks against its victim&#8217;s network.</p>\n<p>Some of the demanded ransoms reached into the millions of dollars. Maze reportedly <a href=\"https://www.bleepingcomputer.com/news/security/maze-ransomware-demands-6-million-ransom-from-southwire/\">demanded $6 million</a> from one Georgia-based wire and cable manufacturer, and <a href=\"https://news.sophos.com/en-us/2020/09/22/mtr-casebook-blocking-a-15-million-maze-ransomware-attack/\">$15 million</a> from one unnamed organization after the group encrypted its network. But after COVID-19 was declared a pandemic in March, Maze — as well as other ransomware groups — promised to <a href=\"https://www.bleepingcomputer.com/news/security/ransomware-gangs-to-stop-attacking-health-orgs-during-pandemic/\">not target hospitals</a> and medical facilities.</p>\n<p>But security experts aren&#8217;t celebrating just yet. After all, ransomware gangs are still criminal enterprises, many of which are driven by profit.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2068836\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2068836\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2068836\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/maze-ransomware-note.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"679\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/maze-ransomware-note.jpg 2542w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/maze-ransomware-note.jpg?resize=150,99 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/maze-ransomware-note.jpg?resize=300,199 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/maze-ransomware-note.jpg?resize=768,509 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/maze-ransomware-note.jpg?resize=680,451 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/maze-ransomware-note.jpg?resize=1536,1019 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/maze-ransomware-note.jpg?resize=2048,1358 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/maze-ransomware-note.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2068836\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">A statement by the Maze ransomware group, claiming it has shut down. <strong>Screenshot:</strong> TechCrunch</p></div></p>\n<p>&#8220;Obviously, Maze’s claims should be taken with a very, very small pinch of salt,&#8221; said Brett Callow, a ransomware expert and threat analyst at security firm <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/emsisoft\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"emsisoft\">Emsisoft <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a>. &#8220;It&#8217;s certainly possible that the group feels they have made enough money to be able to close shop and sail off into the sunset. However, it&#8217;s also possible — and probably more likely — that they&#8217;ve decided to rebrand.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Callow said the group&#8217;s apparent disbanding leaves open questions about the Maze group&#8217;s connections and involvement with other groups. &#8220;As Maze was an affiliate operation, their partners in crime are unlikely to retire and will instead simply align themselves with another group,&#8221; he said.</p>\n<p>Maze denied that it was a &#8220;cartel&#8221; of ransomware groups in its statement, but experts disagree. Steve Ragan, a security researcher at Akamai, said Maze was known to post on its website data from other ransomware, like Ragnar Locker and the LockBit ransomware-for-hire.</p>\n<p>&#8220;For them to pretend now that there was no team-up or cartel is just plain backwards. Clearly these groups were working together on many levels,&#8221; said Ragan.</p>\n<p>&#8220;The downside to this, and the other significant element, is that nothing will change, Ransomware is still going to be out there,&#8221; said Ragan. &#8220;Criminals are still targeting open access, exposed RDP [remote desktop protocol] and VPN portals, and still sending malicious emails with malicious attachments in the hope of infecting unsuspecting victims on the internet,&#8221; he said.</p>\n<p>Jeremy Kennelly at <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/fireeye\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"fireeye\">FireEye&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> Mandiant threat intelligence unit said that while the Maze brand may be dead, its operators are likely not gone for good.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We assess with high confidence that many of the individuals and groups that collaborated to enable the Maze ransomware service will likely continue to engage in similar operations — either working to support existing ransomware services or supporting novel operations in the future,&#8221; said Kennelly.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"UPsHIdT8yH\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/01/08/as-ransomware-gets-craftier-companies-must-start-thinking-creatively/\">As ransomware gets craftier, companies must start thinking creatively</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;As ransomware gets craftier, companies must start thinking creatively&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/01/08/as-ransomware-gets-craftier-companies-must-start-thinking-creatively/embed/#?secret=UPsHIdT8yH\" fintech","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2068986","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/paypal\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"paypal\">PayPal&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> stock is down in after-hours trading after <a href=\"https://s1.q4cdn.com/633035571/files/doc_financials/2020/q3/Q3-20-PayPal-Earnings-Release.pdf\">reporting third-quarter earnings</a> that beat expectations. It&#8217;s not immediately clear why PayPal is losing ground, although it could stem from retail investor having higher expectations than what analysts estimated for the high-flying company.</p>\n<p>Despite failing to delight the investing public, it’s possible to see continued strength for the broader fintech industry in its results.</p>\n<p>PayPal reported revenues of $5.46 billion and adjusted earnings per share of $1.07 in the third quarter of 2020. Both were <a href=\"https://finance.yahoo.com/quote/PYPL/analysis/\">ahead</a> of analyst expectations of $5.43 billion and $0.94, respectively.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Turning away from PayPal&#8217;s income statement, it detailed a wealth of fintech-specific data to parse, including results that appear to indicate that <a href=\"https://news.crunchbase.com/news/survey-says-fintech-on-the-rise-during-covid/\">rising consumer usage of fintech products during the pandemic</a> is continuing. For example, the company reported what it described as the &#8220;strongest&#8221; pace of growth in its total payment volume in its history.</p>\n<p>In numerical terms, PayPal processed $247 billion, up 38% from the year-ago quarter, and 4 billion payments, up 30% across the same time frame. For startups that want to facilitate consumer or business payment volume, that&#8217;s good news; their market is growing quickly.</p>\n<p>PayPal also raised its full-year payment volume growth estimates for the year from the &#8220;high 20s&#8221; in percentage terms <a href=\"https://s1.q4cdn.com/633035571/files/doc_financials/2020/q2/Q2-20-PayPal-Earnings-Release-7.30.20.pdf\">in its Q2 earnings</a> to &#8220;approximately 30%&#8221; as of the end of Q3 2020, adding to the good fintech news.</p>\n<p>Other metrics that PayPal reported were similarly bullish, including Venmo payment processing volume rising 61% compared to the year-ago period to $44 billion. That year-over-year gain was an acceleration from 52% growth in Q2, again compared to year-ago periods.</p>\n<p>Finally, PayPal&#8217;s &#8220;payment transactions per active account on a trailing twelve month basis&#8221; grew to 40.1 from 39.2 in the second quarter. Including <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/11/20/paypal-to-acquire-shopping-and-rewards-platform-honey-for-4-billion/\">the Honey deal that closed earlier this year</a>, the number jumps to 41.7.</p>\n<p>The results imply winsome e-commerce activity and consumer fintech appetite.</p>\n<p>It&#8217;s too soon to learn much about from PayPal&#8217;s new Venmo credit card, and its cryptocurrency efforts that bolstered the price of bitcoin recently. But core consumer affinity for fintech, viewed through the lens of PayPal&#8217;s earnings, looks strong.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/bsW-zVukSjM\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 02 Nov 2020 22:29:31 +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI","linkMd5":"4d2f0e3ed91ecfee6d9725a09f15c62a","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn22@2020_6/2020/11/03/05-31-20-196_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","destWidth":59,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":990,"destBytes":324,"author":"Alex Wilhelm","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn22@2020_6/2020/11/03/05-31-20-196_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn96@2020_5/2020/11/03/05-31-35-908_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn52@2020_4/2020/11/03/05-31-34-882_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=bsW-zVukSjM:M5HVL54Ko3Q:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn16@2020_2/2020/11/03/05-31-36-012_6c0f9db83eaf9fd8.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=bsW-zVukSjM:M5HVL54Ko3Q:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn79@2020_5/2020/11/03/05-31-34-685_4a6a4067abd115ef.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn35@2020_5/2020/11/03/05-31-35-960_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/bsW-zVukSjM":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn79@2020_4/2020/11/03/05-31-34-732_de9c2f15e9e9e949.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1604381479576},{"createdTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:19","updatedTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:19","title":"YC-backed nonprofit VotingWorks wants to rebuild trust in election systems through open source","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2068865","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">I know it will come as a shock to you as a reader of the news, but there is an election this week. Well, tomorrow actually.</p>\n<p>It’s the rare election where the logistics of the election itself seem to be increasingly dominating the discussion. Not since the Florida recount of 2000 have pollsters, analysts and party lawyers been so fixated on the mechanics of ballots. Which ballots will be counted? Will the Post Office deliver mail in time? How many drop-off boxes are authorized by county? Will the voting machines leave an auditable paper trail?</p>\n<p>Voting in America is a complex affair — while presidential elections are national in scope, the actual logistics of ballots and votes are decided locally: not just state by state, but often also county by county. That can create huge variation in the systems at play — but it also means that a small county in rural Mississippi can be a test case for the rest of the nation in how to get voting done right.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>That’s at least what <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/votingworks\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"votingworks\">VotingWorks <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> is banking on.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://voting.works\">VotingWorks</a> is a non-partisan, nonprofit startup that graduated from YC in its winter batch last year with the twin goals of improving the technology that underpins elections through more affordable and secure voting systems as well as using modern statistical science to improve the quality and efficiency of voter audits. The nonprofit scoured the country looking for a testbed, and eventually found Choctaw County in Mississippi, a rural jurisdiction just shy of 10,000 residents who were willing to try VotingWorks’ system in their election.</p>\n<p>Matt Pasternack, who along with Ben Adida co-founded the organization, said that the existing voting machines there were “ancient” and didn’t have a paper audit trail. “We found one county that was so eager to get rid of these ancient machines that they said, ‘Yes, we want to, we want to use this new thing you guys are building,’ ” Pasternack said.</p>\n<p>What VotingWorks built is quite competitive. First, the company used existing hardware rather than designing custom-built hardware that can be extraordinarily costly given that the machines are rarely used in the U.S., which has quadrennial elections for many offices. Second, the organization’s software is <a href=\"https://github.com/votingworks\">posted as open source on GitHub</a>. That made the machines more open and verifiable than competitors, and also available at a lower price point.</p>\n<p>Pasternack and Adida met while working together at Clever, the API middleware platform that today could be dubbed the “Plaid of education,” designed to help app developers connect to the data stored in hundreds of student information systems. Pasternack noted that he was employee number one, and the two talked about politics and elections over the years and eventually saw an opportunity to enter the market with the 2018 midterms.</p>\n<p>The team went through YC in early 2019. With Choctaw County’s push to replace their machines, VotingWorks managed to get its machines in their hands by August for the November 2019 election, when statewide offices, including the governor and attorney general, were up for election. The machines were used in 13 precincts.</p>\n<p>Adida said that the company moved very fast, but the in-field experience was crucial for improving their machines. He noted that one thing the crew learned is that on election day, poll workers have to set up each machine in the morning before the first rush of voters. The speed of setup is crucial for getting poll places ready, and so VotingWorks optimized how many steps were involved in setting up each ballot machine. “With our machines, you put it on a table, you pop open the case, and you run the checklist. It takes about two-to-three minutes, compared to 30 [minutes] … and so the poll workers were raving about it,” he said.</p>\n<p>Pasternack also added that in a rural county like Choctaw, power constraints added their own complexity. Precincts could be remarkably underpowered, and too many voting machines on one electrical circuit could blow out the entire precinct — preventing anyone from voting.</p>\n<p>Since then, the organization’s technology has expanded to about 10% of Mississippi counties, partly driven by the need this year for color printing technology. The state is voting on changing its state flag to remove the imprint of the Confederate flag, and voters have to see the new flags in color on the ballot. Pasternack said that their on-demand printing technology is both efficient and much more affordable per ballot.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2068882\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2068882\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2068882\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/MS-Flag.png?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"211\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/MS-Flag.png 3211w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/MS-Flag.png?resize=150,47 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/MS-Flag.png?resize=300,93 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/MS-Flag.png?resize=768,238 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/MS-Flag.png?resize=680,211 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/MS-Flag.png?resize=1536,477 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/MS-Flag.png?resize=2048,636 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/MS-Flag.png?resize=50,16 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2068882\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Mississippi&#8217;s Existing Flag and proposed new flag that will be on the state&#8217;s ballot tomorrow. Images via Wikipedia. New flag credited on Wikipedia to Rocky Vaughn, Sue Anna Joe and Kara Giles.</p></div></p>\n<p>Outside of the machines, the organization is building up its audit software to make audits more statistically accurate and cheaper to conduct, and also developing systems for processing absentee ballots better. Each of these technologies work independently of one another — Adida stressed that “An important trait of a modern voting system is that it&#8217;s modular. You can use our auditing system with any standard tabulator. You absolutely don’t need to be using VotingWorks.” Its tech is now used in several additional states in addition to Mississippi, including crucial swing states Michigan and Pennsylvania.</p>\n<p>The nonprofit has a critical day tomorrow, but then the future beckons. With so much focus on election logistics this year, the hope is that more counties and states will begin to think through better, more robust systems to operate their elections. “We want a world where the foundation of democracy is publicly owned, so having open-source software shepherded by a nonprofit organization — it feels like a better democracy to me,” Adida said.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/2020-election/\"><img src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/us-2020-election-footer.png\" /></a></p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a Newell","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2068886","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/rocket-lab\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"rocket-lab\">Rocket Lab&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> next mission will put dozens of satellites into orbit using the launch company&#8217;s Kick Stage &#8220;space tug,&#8221; as well as a 3D-printed garden gnome from Valve Software&#8217;s Gabe Newell. The latter is a test of a new manufacturing technique, but also a philanthropic endeavor from the gaming industry legend.</p>\n<p>Scheduled for no earlier than November 15 (or 16 at the New Zealand launch site), the as-yet-unnamed launch — Rocket Lab gives all of their missions cheeky names — will be the company&#8217;s &#8220;most diverse ever,&#8221; it said in a press release.</p>\n<p>A total of 30 satellites will be deployed using Rocket Lab&#8217;s own Kick Stage deployment platform, which like other &#8220;space tugs&#8221; detaches from the second stage once a certain preliminary orbit is reached and then delivers its payloads each at their own unique trajectory. That&#8217;s the most individual satellites every taken up at once by Rocket Lab.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Twenty-four of them are <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/swarm-technologies\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"swarm-technologies\">Swarm Technologies&#8217; <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> tiny SpaceBEEs, the sandwich-sized communications satellites it will be using to power a <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/29/swarm-prices-out-its-orbital-iot-networks-hardware-and-services/\">low-cost, low-bandwidth global network for Internet of Things devices</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"3EhlTNW0lX\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/29/swarm-prices-out-its-orbital-iot-networks-hardware-and-services/\">Swarm prices out its orbital IoT network&#8217;s hardware and services</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Swarm prices out its orbital IoT network&#8217;s hardware and services&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/29/swarm-prices-out-its-orbital-iot-networks-hardware-and-services/embed/#?secret=3EhlTNW0lX\" data-secret=\"3EhlTNW0lX\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>The most unusual payload, however, is certainly &#8220;Gnome Chompski,&#8221; whose passage was paid by Valve president Newell: a 3D-printed figure that will remain attached to the Kick Stage until it burns up on reentry. The figure, a replica of an item from the popular Half-Life series of PC games, was made by Weta Workshop, the effects studio behind Lord of the Rings and many other films. It&#8217;s both a test of a potentially useful new component printing technique and &#8220;an homage to the innovation and creativity of gamers worldwide.&#8221;</p>\n<p>More importantly, Newell will donate a dollar to Starship Children&#8217;s Hospital for every viewer of the launch, so you&#8217;ll definitely want to tune in for this one. (I&#8217;m waiting to find out more from Newell, if possible.)</p>\n<p>The launch will also deliver satellites for TriSept, Unseenlabs and the Auckland Space Institute — the last will be New Zealand&#8217;s first student-built spacecraft.</p>\n<p>Rocket Lab has worked hard to make its launch platform all-in-one, so prospective customers don&#8217;t have to shop around for various services or components. Ideally, the company&#8217;s CEO has said, anyone should be able to come to the company with the bare-bones payload and the rest is taken care of.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2039801\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/photon-lab.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2039801\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2039801\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/photon-lab.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"580\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/photon-lab.jpg 1662w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/photon-lab.jpg?resize=150,85 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/photon-lab.jpg?resize=300,170 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/photon-lab.jpg?resize=768,435 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/photon-lab.jpg?resize=680,385 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/photon-lab.jpg?resize=1536,871 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/photon-lab.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2039801\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Rocket Lab</p></div></p>\n<p>&#8220;Small satellite operators shouldn’t have to compromise on orbits when flying on a rideshare mission, and we’re excited to provide tailored access to space for 30 satellites on this mission. It’s why we created the Kick Stage to enable custom orbits on every mission, and eliminate the added complexity, time, and cost of having to develop your own spacecraft propulsion or using a third-party space tug,&#8221; Beck said in the press release.</p>\n<p>Rocket Lab recently <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/03/rocket-lab-secretly-launched-its-very-first-satellite-first-light/\">launched its own home-grown satellite, First Light</a>, to show that getting to orbit doesn&#8217;t have be such a &#8220;pain in the butt,&#8221; as Beck put it then.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"AJ8n2Z600r\"><p><a
